Ruling on Mouse in a Well: 20 Buckets
Ruling with proof for small animals in a well

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for small animals dying in a well and apply the condition that swelling escalates the ruling.

Core Idea
A mouse in a well requires exactly 20 buckets — a fixed tradition, not a variable based on impurity.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a large animal like a chicken requires full removal of well water. Here, the ruling scales down for small animals such as mice and rats. The Hanafi school prescribes a fixed quota of 20 buckets for this category, based on a narration from the Tabi'i 'Ata. The key condition is that the animal did not swell; if it did, the ruling escalates to full removal. This lesson anchors the numerical ruling for the smallest animal category.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animal category
The text mentions 'mouse or similar' (فارة او نحوها). This includes small terrestrial animals that do not have flowing blood (like mice, rats, lizards, etc.) that die without swelling.
Similar animals are those comparable in size and fluid content.
2
State the ruling (20 buckets)
The wajib action is to draw 20 buckets of water. This is the fixed number from the tradition, not a calculation based on impurity.
The number is taken literally as a command indicating obligation.
3
Note the condition: no swelling
If the animal has swollen, the ruling escalates to full removal (as per the prior lesson). The 20-bucket quota only applies when there is no swelling.
Swelling indicates decomposition, which increases impurity.
4
Cite the proof
The evidence is the saying of 'Ata: 'If a rat falls into a well, draw twenty buckets.' This is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
The Hanafi school takes this as a sound basis for the ruling.
5
Compare with other schools
Unlike the Hanafis, the Shafi'i school does not prescribe fixed numbers; they look for change in water properties (color, taste, smell). This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The practical consequence: Hanafis always draw 20 buckets; Shafi'is may require less or more depending on change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان مات فيها فارة او نحوها لزم نزح عشرين دلوا. (۲۸) وان مات فيها فارة او نحوها لزم نزح عشرين دلوا . وجه : (۱) عن عطاء قال اذا وقع الجرذ في البئر نزح منها عشرون دلوا - ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۱۹۸۷افی الفارة و الدجاجة وأشباههما تقع في البئر ، ج اول ص ۱۴۹، نمبر ۱۷۱۴) جرز ایک قسم کا چوہا ہے جس کے مرنے سے ہیں ڈول نکالنا لا زم ہوا
And if a mouse or similar dies in it, twenty buckets must be drawn. (28) Ruling: And if a mouse or similar dies in it, twenty buckets must be drawn. Proof: (1) From 'Ata: he said, 'If a rat falls into a well, draw twenty buckets.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) 'Rat' is a type of mouse; its death requires drawing twenty buckets.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling for small animals like mice or rats that die in a well without swelling: 20 buckets are required. The evidence is a saying of 'Ata, a well-known Tabi'i, who explicitly states twenty buckets for a rat. The Hanafi school adopts this as the standard for small animals. The key condition is that the animal did not swell; if it did, the ruling escalates to full removal (as per the first lesson).

Key Terms
فارة (fārah): Mouse, considered a small animal requiring 20 buckets.
جرذ (jurath): Rat, a type of mouse, same ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many buckets must be drawn if a mouse dies in a well without swelling?
A) 20
B) 40
C) 60
D) 200

Key Takeaway
A small animal dying in a well without swelling requires wajib removal of 20 buckets, based on the tradition of 'Ata.

The Ruling on Automatic Purification of Well-Related Items
Ruling with proof on automatic purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that drawing the required amount of water purifies the well, bucket, rope, and hand, and explain the proof from the practice of Ibn al-Zubayr.

Core Idea
Drawing impure water itself purifies all related items – no separate washing needed.

This lesson follows the previous rulings on purifying a well after it becomes impure. The Hanafi school extends the purification not only to the well's water but also to the bucket, rope, and even the hand of the person drawing the water. The rationale is ease (taysir) and the practice of the early Muslims, as recorded in a narration about Zamzam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What does the text say becomes pure? List the items: the well (walls and remaining water), the bucket, the rope, and the hand of the drawer.
The ruling is that they are purified automatically, no extra action.
2
Understand the rationale
Why is separate washing not required? The text mentions hardship (mashaqqah). Hanafi fiqh often removes hardship where possible.
3
Analyze the proof
The proof is a saying of a Companion (qawl sahabi): Ibn al-Zubayr at Zamzam said 'hasbukum' (that is enough) after drawing water. This indicates that the drawing itself suffices for purification.
The proof is zanni in transmission and meaning.
4
Compare with other schools
Note that the Shafi'i school may require separate purification of items that were directly contaminated, creating a practical difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكان ذلك طهارة للبئر والدلو والرشاء ويد المستقى. (۲۹)وكان ذلك طهارة للبئر والدلو والرشاء ويد المستقى. تشریح : جتنا پانی نکالنا لا زم تھا کنواں سے اتنا پانی نکال دیا، تو اسی سے کنواں کی دیوار، اس کا باقی پانی نکالنے والا ڈول، رسی ، اور نکالنے والے کا ہاتھ پاک ہو گیا، اس کو مزید دھونے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس کو دوبارہ دھونا ایک مشکل کام ہے اس لئے نکالتے ہی سب کو پاک قرار دے دیا گیا۔ (۲) اس قول صحابی میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن عطاء ان حبشيا وقع فى زمزم فمات قال فأمر ابن الزبير أن ينزف ماء زمزم قال فجعل الماء لا ينقطع قال فنظروا فاذا عين تنبع من قبل الحجر الاسود قال فقال ابن الزبير حسبكم ۔(مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، ۱۹۸ فى الفارة والدجاجة وأشباههما تقع في البئر ، ج اول ص ۱۵۰ نمبر (۱۷۲) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ اتنا پانی نکال دیا، بس اتنا ہی کافی ہے، جس سے اشارہ ہے کہ اسی نکالنے سے ڈول، رسی، کنویں کی دیوار، اور نکالنے والے کا ہاتھ پاک ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ اس کے بعد کسی چیز کو دھونے کا حکم نہیں دیا۔ لغت الرشاء: ری۔ استسقی : استقاء سے مشتق ہے پانی سیراب کرنا، یہاں مراد ہے پانی نکالنا۔
And that [drawing of water] is purification for the well, the bucket, the rope, and the hand of the one drawing water. (29) Ruling: And that [drawing of water] is purification for the well, the bucket, the rope, and the hand of the one drawing water. Explanation: When the required amount of water is drawn, the well's wall, the remaining water, the bucket, rope, and the drawer's hand become pure without further washing. Proof: (1) Rewashing is a hardship, so they are deemed pure by the act of drawing. (2) Indicated by the saying of a Companion: from 'Ata: a black man fell into Zamzam and died; Ibn al-Zubayr ordered the water to be drawn... then he said, 'That is enough for you.' This indicates that the drawing itself suffices, and no additional washing is commanded. Lexicon: al-risha': rope; istasqa: derived from istiqā', to draw water.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage states that the removal of the required amount of water from the well automatically purifies all items that have come into contact with the impure water: the well itself (its walls and remaining water), the bucket, the rope, and even the hand of the person drawing water. The rationale is that requiring separate washing would create hardship (mashaqqah). This is supported by the practice of Ibn al-Zubayr at Zamzam, where after drawing water, no further washing was ordered. The lesson applies to all the previous rulings: once the prescribed number of buckets are drawn, everything is pure.

Key Terms
رشاء (rishā'): Rope used to draw water from the well.
يد المستقى (yad al-mustaqrī): The hand of the person drawing water.
طهارة (tahārah): Purification, in this context the state of ritual purity of the well and related items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, what happens to the bucket and rope when the required amount of water is drawn from an impure well?
A) They become pure automatically.
B) They must be washed separately with pure water.
C) They remain impure until left to dry.
D) Only the bucket becomes pure.

Key Takeaway
Drawing the required amount of water from a well automatically purifies the well, bucket, rope, and hand – no separate washing needed.

Minor Dung Does Not Impurify the Well
Ruling: well not impurified by small dung

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the purity of a well when small amounts of animal dung fall into it.

Core Idea
Small amounts of dry dung are pardoned; the well remains pure.

This lesson clarifies a practical taharah ruling: what happens when animal dung falls into a well? The Hanafi position is that minimal amounts are overlooked due to the principle of 'afw (pardon). This eases daily life, especially in agricultural settings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The text states the well does not become impure (la tuanjis al-bi'r) by small amounts of dung (ba'r, rawth, khutha).
This is a fixed Hanafi ruling.
2
Recognise the Types of Dung
Ba'r is camel/sheep dung, rawth is horse/donkey droppings, khutha is mixed manure. All are treated similarly.
All are solid, dry impurities.
3
Understand the Condition
The exception 'illa' indicates that if the dung is so abundant that the bucket brings up only dung, the well becomes impure.
Threshold is based on overwhelming change.
4
Apply the Principle of 'Afw
The Hanafi school pardons minor impurities in large bodies of water, especially when they are solid and not dissolved.
This differs from other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تنجس البئر بالبعر والروث والخثى الا وجه (1) عن ابراهيم في الجرذ او السنور تقع في البئر قال يدلو منها أربعين دلوا_(مصنف ابن ابى شيبة ، باب في الفارة والدجاجة واشباهها تقع في البئر ، ج اول ص ۱۴۹، نمبر ۷۱۳ الطحاوی شریف، باب الماء تقع فيه النجاسة ص ۱۶/مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب البئر تقع فی الدابة ، ج اول ص ۶۴ نمبر ۲۷۲ (۲) عن سلمة بن كهيل في الدجاجة تقع في البئر قال : يستقى منها أربعون دلوا - (مصنف ابن ابى شيبة ، ۱۹۸ فى الفارة والدجاجة وأشباههما تقع في البئر ، ج اول ص ۱۴۹، نمبر ۱۷۱۹) ان دونوں اثروں میں ہے کہ مرغی یا بلی مر جائے تو چالیس ڈول نکالا جائے۔
And the well does not become impure by [small amounts of] dung (ba'r), droppings (rawth), or manure (khuthā') unless its face? Explanation: Then the text gives two narrations from Ibrahim and Salamah ibn Kuhayl about 40 buckets for cat/chicken, which appear to be misplaced. The intended ruling is likely: the well is not impurified by small amounts of dung unless it is abundant and the bucket pulls up only dung.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage appears to state a Hanafi ruling regarding light impurities: the well does not become impure if small amounts of dung (like from animals) fall into it. The condition is that the dung is not so abundant that the bucket brings up nothing but dung. The Arabic text is somewhat garbled, but the meaning is clear from the context of well rulings. The references to 40 buckets are likely from previous lessons and may have been inserted by mistake. The key point is that small quantities of solid dry impurities do not nullify the well's purity; only if they are excessive does the water become impure. This is based on the principle of 'affw (pardon) for minor impurities in large bodies of water.

Key Terms
بعر (ba'r): Dung of camels, sheep, etc., considered a light impurity.
روث (rawth): Droppings of horses, donkeys, etc.
خثى (khuthā): Manure, mixed dung, often from cattle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does dung make a well impure?
A) Whenever any dung falls in.
B) Only when the dung is so abundant that the bucket brings up nothing but dung.
C) Only if the dung dissolves completely.
D) Never, dung is always pure.

Key Takeaway
Small amounts of dry dung are pardoned ('afw) in a well, but if the dung is so abundant that it dominates the water, the well becomes impure.

Drawing 20 Buckets for a Dead Mouse in the Well
Ruling on the amount of water to draw when a dead mouse is found

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for purifying a well when a mouse dies in it and identify the proof cited by the school.

Core Idea
When a mouse dies in a well, drawing twenty buckets of water is obligatory (wajib) for purification.

This lesson presents a clear ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the purification of well water. When a small animal like a mouse dies in a well, a specific amount of water must be drawn to restore purity. The ruling is accompanied by a proof from a narration of the Tabi'i Ata, which the Hanafis rely upon.

Guided Path
1
State the act and ruling
Identify the act (purifying a well after a mouse's death) and the ruling: it is wajib (obligatory) to draw twenty buckets.
The ruling is from the later Hanafi works, consistent with the principles of purification.
2
Identify the condition
Note the condition mentioned: the animal must not be bloated or burst. If it is, more buckets may be required.
Bloating indicates greater contamination.
3
Locate the dalil
Find the proof: a narration from Ata ibn Abi Rabah in Musaddad's narration, saying 'If a rat falls into a well, twenty buckets are drawn from it.'
The source is Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, classified as a qawl sahabi.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The narration explicitly states the number, so the Hanafis adopt it as the standard. The command indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
The proof is zanni in thubut and dalala, but sufficient for obligation.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may require a different amount (e.g., 40 buckets) for the same situation.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان مات فيها فارة او نحوها لزم نزح عشرين دلوا .
ترجمه : (۲۸) اور اگر کنواں میں چوہا ، یا اس جیسا کوئی جانور مر گیا تو ہیں ڈول نکالنا لازم ہوگا۔ تشریح : اگر کنواں میں چوہا مر گیا ہو یا اس جیسا جانور مر گیا ہو، اور پھولا پھٹا نہ ہو تو ہمیں ڈول نکالنے سے کنواں پاک ہو جائے گا وجه : (۱) عن عطاء قال اذا وقع الجرذ في البئر نزح منها عشرون دلوا - ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۱۹۸۷افی الفارة و الدجاجة وأشباههما تقع في البئر ، ج اول ص ۱۴۹، نمبر ۱۷۱۴) جرز ایک قسم کا چوہا ہے جس کے مرنے سے ہیں ڈول نکالنا لا زم ہوا
And if a mouse or the like dies in it, the drawing of twenty buckets becomes obligatory. Translation: (28) And if a mouse or similar animal dies in the well, then drawing 20 buckets is necessary. Explanation: If a mouse or similar animal has died in the well and it is not bloated or burst, then by drawing 20 buckets the well becomes pure. Proof: (1) From Ata who said, 'If a rat falls into a well, twenty buckets are drawn from it' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba). 'Jurz' is a type of large mouse, for whose death drawing 20 buckets is necessary.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the purification of a well when a small animal such as a mouse or rat dies in it. The author states the ruling clearly: it is obligatory to draw twenty buckets of water from the well. The commentary explains that this applies when the animal is not bloated or burst, as a bloated animal would cause greater contamination requiring more water. The proof cited is an athar (tradition) from the Tabi'i Ata ibn Abi Rabah, reported in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, that if a jerboa (large rat) falls into a well, twenty buckets are to be drawn. The word 'جرذ' refers to a large rat or jerboa. The Hanafi school considers this sufficient for purification in such cases.

Key Terms
فارة (fāra): A mouse or rat; a small rodent that may fall into a well.
دلو (dalw): A bucket used to draw water from a well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mouse dies in a well and is found not bloated, how many buckets must be drawn to purify the well according to the Hanafi school?
A) 40 buckets
B) 20 buckets
C) 60 buckets
D) 30 buckets

Key Takeaway
A mouse or similar small animal in a well requires drawing 20 buckets; this is based on the practice of the Tabi'i Ata.

Dung Does Not Pollute the Well Unless Excessive
Ruling with proof on impurity of well water due to dung

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a well becomes impure due to dung and apply the hadith of Bir Badha'a as proof.

Core Idea
A well remains pure despite minor dung until the amount is seen as excessive or every bucket contains dung.

Rural wells often face the problem of animal droppings falling in. The Hanafi school, citing the hadith of Bir Badha'a, rules that such impurities do not automatically nullify the water's purity. Only when the dung is so abundant that it is considered a lot or appears in every bucket does the well become impure. This lesson unpacks the textual proof and the threshold for impurity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The act in question is the well water. By default, the water is pure (tahir) and permissible to use for wudu and other purposes.
The Hanafi school heavily relies on the principle that abundant water remains pure unless it changes in taste, color, or smell.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Bir Badha'a, where the Prophet declared water pure despite various impurities being thrown in.
This hadith is a narrated in Sunan al-Tirmidhi and is considered sahih by many scholars.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's statement 'Water is pure and nothing makes it impure' indicates that minor, common impurities do not nullify purity unless they are excessive.
The Hanafi usul holds that this general text (amm) remains binding until a specific exclusion (takhsis) is proven.
4
Note the threshold for impurity
The well becomes impure if the observer considers the dung to be a lot or if every bucket drawn contains a piece of dung. This threshold is based on customary judgment.
The threshold is subjective ('urfi) and varies by context, but the key is that the impurity is no longer incidental.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a well in a camel pen. A few droppings fall in daily. The water remains pure. But if dung floats in every bucket, the water is impure.
This application highlights the balance between necessity and purity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تنجس البئر بالبعر والروث والخثى الا ان يستكثره الناظر او أن لا يخلو دلو عن بعرة .
ترجمه : (۳۰) اور تھوڑی سی مینگنی، اور لید اور، گوبر سے کنواں ناپاک نہیں ہوگا مگر یہ کہ دیکھنے والا اس کو زیادہ سمجھے، اور کوئی ڈول مینگنی سے خالی نہ جائے [ تواب نا پاک ہوگا ]
تشریح : اصل قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ دیہات میں جو نجاست روز کنواں میں گر سکتی ہو اس میں مجبوری ہے اس لئے تھوڑی سی نجاست گرنے سے ناپاک نہیں قرار دیا، ہں اتنی نجاست گر جائے کہ اب دیکھنے والا بہت زیادہ سمجھے، مثلا ہر ڈول میں ایک دو مینگنی آنے لگے تو اب کنواں کو نا پاک قرار دیا جائے گا، اس سے پہلے نہیں۔
وجه : بیر بضاعہ کی حدیث میں ایسا لگتا ہے کہ روز مرہ کی نجاست گرتی رہتی تھی پھر بھی اس کو پاک قرار دیا۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابي سعيد الخدري قال : قيل يا رسول الله أنتوضا من بئر بضاعة ، وهي بئر يلقى فيها الحيض و لحوم الكلاب و النتن ؟ فقال رسول الله لا لا لا له : ان الماء طهور لا ينجسه شيء - ترندى شریف ، باب ما جاء أن الماء لا ينجسه شیء ی ۲۱ نمبر ۶۶)
And the well does not become impure by camel dung, animal dung, or dry dung unless the observer considers it a lot or no bucket is free from a dung piece. Translation: (30) And a small amount of dung, animal droppings, and manure does not make the well impure unless the observer considers it a lot or no bucket can escape a dung piece [then it becomes impure]. Explanation: The basic principle is that in rural areas, impurity that may fall daily into the well is excused, so a small amount of impurity does not render it impure. However, if so much impurity falls that the observer considers it a lot, for example every bucket contains one or two dung pieces, then the well is ruled impure; before that it is not. Proof: In the hadith of Bir Badha'a, it appears that daily impurities used to fall but it was still declared pure. The hadith: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: It was asked, 'O Messenger of Allah, can we perform wudu from Bir Badha'a, a well into which menstrual cloths, dog meat, and foul things are thrown?' The Messenger of Allah said: 'Water is pure and nothing makes it impure.' (Tirmidhi)
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of well water becoming impure due to animal dung. The ruling states that the well does not become impure by a small amount of camel dung (ba'r), animal dung (rawth), or dry dung (khithiy). However, if the observer considers the amount excessive, or if every bucket drawn contains some dung, then the well becomes impure. The commentary explains the principle of necessity ('udhr) for rural wells where such impurities often fall due to animals passing by. As long as the quantity is small and occasional, the water remains pure. The proof cited is the famous hadith of Bir Badha'a, where the well contained various impurities yet the Prophet declared water inherently pure. The Hanafi school uses this to establish that a small amount of common impurities does not nullify the purity of abundant water.

Key Terms
البعر (al-ba'r): Camel dung, specifically the droppings of camels.
الروث (al-rawth): Dung of horses, mules, donkeys, and similar animals.
الخثى (al-khithiy): Dried dung used as fuel, also general manure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a well become impure due to dung falling into it?
A) If any single dung piece falls into the well
B) Only if the dung causes a change in the water's taste, color, or smell
C) If the observer considers the dung to be a lot or every bucket drawn contains a dung piece
D) Never, because dung is not considered impure

Key Takeaway
A well remains pure despite common impurities unless they are excessive, based on the hadith 'Water is pure and nothing makes it impure.'

Pigeon Droppings and Bloodless Animals Do Not Spoil Water
Ruling that bird droppings and dead bloodless animals do not spoil well water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two categories of substances that do not spoil well water according to the Hanafi school, and explain the basis for leniency using the principle of umum al-balwa.

Core Idea
Pigeon droppings and dead bloodless animals do not spoil water because 'umum al-balwa makes impurity impractical.

In daily life, it is common for bird droppings or small insects to fall into a well. The Hanafi school, recognizing the difficulty of avoiding such occurrences, rules that the water remains pure. This lesson examines the specific cases of pigeon and sparrow droppings, as well as any animal without flowing blood, and the evidence from the Tabi'een.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being ruled upon? The ruling is that water does not become impure (spoiled) when certain substances fall into it. Specifically, droppings of pigeons and sparrows, and the dead bodies of animals without flowing blood.
The hukm level is tahir (pure) – the water remains pure.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites statements from the Tabi'een (successors), particularly al-Hasan al-Basri. The key narration describes a bird dropping excrement on al-Hasan, who merely wiped it off without washing, indicating he considered it not impure.
The proof type is Qawl Sahabi (sayings of the Companions, here Tabi'een).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this narration prove the ruling? Al-Hasan's action of wiping instead of washing shows that in his view, the droppings were not najis (impure) since if they were, he would have washed. Thus, bird droppings are not considered impurity.
This is a practical demonstration of the ruling.
4
Note the underlying principle
The reason for leniency is 'umum al-balwa (widespread occurrence) and difficulty of prevention. It is very hard to keep birds and tiny creatures out of water sources, so the law accommodates this necessity.
This principle is used in many Hanafi rulings on impurity.
5
Evaluate cross-madhab status
This ruling is mukhtalaf fih (disputed). Other schools may consider bird droppings najis and spoiling water. The Hanafi position is based on the evidence and the principle of ease.
Understanding the difference helps in practicing with confidence.

ترجمہ : (۳۱) اور کبوتر اور چڑیا کی بیٹ سے پانی فاسد [ خراب نہیں ہوگا اور پانی میں بلاخون والی چیز کے مرنے سے بھی فاسد نہیں ہوگا، مثلا مینڈک اور مچھلی اور پانی کے حیوانات ، اور مچھر اور کھی اور بھڑ اور بچھو۔

وجه : (۱) اس قول تابعی میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن الحسن قال : سقطت هائمة على الحسن فذرقت عليه فقال له بعض القوم : نأتيك بماء تغسله فقال : لا ، و جعل يمسحه عنه ، (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۱۴۵ الذی یصلی و فی ثوبه خرء الطير ، ج اول ص ۱۱۰ نمبر ۶ ۱۲۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ پرندے کی بیٹ نا پاک نہیں ہے۔ (۲) عن الحسن في رجل صلى فلما قضى صلاته أبصر فى ثوبه خرء دجاج فقال انما هو طير - مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب فی خرء الدجاج، ج اول، ص ۱۱، نمبر ۱۲۵۹) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ مرغی کی بیٹ میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ (۳) عن حماد انه كره ذرق الدجاج - ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب فی خرء الدجاج ، ج اول ص ۱۱۱، نمبر ۱۲۶۰) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ مرغی کی بیٹ مکروہ ہے۔ (۴) عن الحسن انه كان يرخص فى ابوال الخفافيش (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب فی بول الخفاش ، ج اول ص ۱۱۰، نمبر (۱۳۴۸) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ چمگادڑ کے پیشاب میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
And water is not spoiled by the droppings of a pigeon or sparrow, nor by the death of something that has no blood in it, such as fish, frog, aquatic animals, bug, fly, wasp, and scorpion. Translation: (31) And the water does not become spoiled due to the droppings of a pigeon or sparrow, nor due to the death of a bloodless creature, e.g., frog, fish, aquatic animals, mosquito, insect, wasp, and scorpion. Explanation: Two types of creatures are mentioned here whose falling into the well does not make the water impure. Some of them would normally cause impurity but due to necessity, leniency is granted. The first type is the droppings of pigeons and sparrows: their falling does not make the well impure. Proof: (1) From al-Hasan: A bird dropped excrement on him, and someone offered to bring water to wash it, but he said no and wiped it away. This shows bird droppings are not impure. (2) From al-Hasan regarding a man who prayed and after prayer saw chicken droppings on his garment: he said, 'It is just a bird.' (3) From Hammad: he disliked chicken droppings (i.e., considered it makruh). (4) From al-Hasan: he permitted the urine of bats.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage addresses two specific exceptions to water impurity. First, the droppings of pigeons and sparrows do not spoil the water, even though they are technically impure. Second, animals that have no flowing blood (i.e., their blood does not flow when cut) such as fish, frogs, aquatic animals, mosquitoes, flies, wasps, and scorpions—if they die in the water, the water remains pure. The commentary explains that normally such things might make water impure, but due to the difficulty of avoiding them, the law grants leniency. The proofs cited are statements from the Tabi'een: al-Hasan al-Basri considered bird droppings not impure, and similarly for chicken droppings. Hammad considered chicken droppings as makruh (disliked), not impure. Also, bat urine was permitted by al-Hasan. These show the lenient position of the Hanafi school on these matters.

Key Terms
خرء (kharʼ): Droppings, excrement of birds and animals.
مالا دم له (mā lā dama lahu): Creatures that have no flowing blood, such as insects, fish, and reptiles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A chicken
B) A fish
C) A dog
D) A cat

Key Takeaway
Pigeon droppings and dead bloodless animals do not make water impure due to the principle of widespread difficulty (umum al-balwa).

Well Water Purity: Bird Droppings and Animals Without Blood
Ruling-with-proof on two categories of impurities that do not spoil well water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two categories of impurities that do not spoil well water according to the Hanafi school and cite the primary proofs (hadith and athar) for each.

Core Idea
Necessity and absence of flowing blood keep well water pure despite common impurities.

Village wells often receive bird droppings and dead insects. Rather than declaring the water impure, the Hanafi school holds that water remains pure for two categories: (1) droppings of domesticated birds like pigeons and sparrows, excused due to necessity, and (2) animals without flowing blood (e.g., fish, flies, scorpions) because impurity is tied to blood. This lesson examines the proofs from hadith and the statements of the Salaf that support this lenient ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the passage to identify the two types of impurities that do not spoil water. One involves bird droppings, the other involves dead animals without flowing blood.
The categories are explicitly listed in the translation.
2
Understand the istiksar principle
The passage opens with a general rule: if impurities are so excessive that every bucket brings dung, the well becomes impure. Otherwise, minor impurities are overlooked due to necessity.
This threshold is based on the hadith of Bir Bada'ah.
3
Examine the proofs for bird droppings
The author cites statements from Hasan al-Basri and Hammad showing that bird droppings (including chicken) are either pure or at most makruh, not najis.
These are athar (sayings of the Tabi'un).
4
Examine the proofs for animals without blood
Key hadiths: (a) 'Every food and drink into which falls an animal without blood... it is lawful to eat, drink and perform wudu with it.' (b) 'Seawater is pure, its dead are lawful.' (c) 'If a fly falls into your vessel, immerse it completely...' These establish that such creatures do not render water impure.
The fly hadith is particularly strong because immersion would not be commanded if it made the water impure.
5
Recognize the role of necessity
The cat hadith shows that even a creature with flowing blood (cat) is excused due to necessity, illustrating the principle that necessity brings ease.
This overarching principle supports the leniency for bird droppings and insects.

اصول : ضرورت کی وجہ سے سہولت ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس حدیث سے یہ اصول مترشح ہوتا ہے۔عن كبشة بـنــت كعب بن مالک ان ابا قتادة دخل عليها قالت فسكبت له وضوء ا قالت فجاءت هرة تشرب فأصغى لها الاناء حتى شربت ، قالت كبشة فرأنى انظر اليه فقال أتعجبين يا ابنة اخى ؟ فقلت نعم قال ان رسول الله علم قال انها ليست بنجس انما هي من الطوافين عليكم والطوافات ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی سوراکھر ق ص ۲۷ نمبر ۹۲ ابوداؤد شریف، باب سؤر الهرة ، ص۱۲، نمبر ۷۵) بلی کا گوشت حرام ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھانا پاک ہونا چاہئے لیکن ضرورت کی وجہ سے اس کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہوا
Chapter on issues of the well: that the onlooker considers it excessive or that the bucket is never free of a dung pellet. (31) Water is not spoiled by the droppings of a pigeon and sparrow, nor by the death of an animal that has no blood in it, such as fish, frog, aquatic animals, bedbug, fly, hornet, and scorpion. Commentary: The basic principle is that the impurities that can fall into a well in villages are a matter of necessity, so a small amount of impurity does not render it impure. However, if so much impurity falls that the onlooker considers it excessive, e.g., every bucket brings one or two pellets, then the well is declared impure; before that, not. Proof: In the hadith of Bir Buda'ah, it seems that impurities were falling daily, yet it was declared pure. The hadith: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: It was said, O Messenger of Allah, should we perform wudu from Bir Buda'ah, a well into which are thrown menstrual cloths, dog meat, and stinking things? He said: Water is pure, nothing makes it impure. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja' anna al-ma' la yanjusuhu shay', no. 66) The hadith indicates that daily impurities fell, so due to necessity it was declared pure. Lexicon: 'bahr' = bird droppings; 'rut' = dung; 'anfi' = dung; 'dalu' = bucket. Translation: (31) Pigeon and sparrow droppings do not spoil water, nor does the death of an animal without blood, e.g., frog, fish, aquatic animals, mosquito, fly? , hornet, scorpion. Commentary: Two types of animals are described whose falling into a well does not make the water impure. Among them are some that would normally render impure, but due to necessity leniency is given. [1] First type: droppings of pigeon and sparrow; their falling does not make the well impure. Proof: (1) The saying of the Tabi'i: From Hasan: A bird dropped excrement on him; someone offered to bring water to wash it; he said no and wiped it off. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 6125) This shows bird droppings are not impure. (2) From Hasan about a man who prayed then saw chicken droppings on his garment; he said it is just a bird. (Musannaf, Bab fi khari al-dajaj, no. 1259) This indicates no harm. (3) From Hammad that he disliked chicken droppings. (Musannaf, no. 1260) This indicates it is makruh. (4) From Hasan that he allowed bat urine. (Musannaf, Bab fi baul al-khuffash, no. 1348) This indicates no harm. [2] Second type: Animals with no blood; their falling and dying in water does not render it impure, e.g., fish, frog, flea, fly, hornet, scorpion. Proof: (1) This issue is based on the principle that flowing blood is impure; hence animals without flowing blood do not make water impure. The hadith: The Messenger of Allah said: O Salman, every food and drink into which falls an animal without blood and dies therein, it is lawful to eat, drink, and perform wudu with it. (Darqutni, Bab kull ta'am waq'at fihi dabbatun laysa laha dam, no. 81; Bayhaqi, Bab ma la nafsa lahu sa'ilatun idha mata fi al-ma' al-qalil, no. 1193) This hadith indicates water is not impure. (2) Regarding fish: Abu Hurairah said a man asked: O Messenger of Allah, we go to sea and carry little water; if we perform wudu with it we become thirsty; can we perform wudu with seawater? He said: Its water is pure, its dead are lawful. (Abu Dawud, Bab al-wudu' bi ma' al-bahr, no. 83; Tirmidhi, no. 69) This indicates dead fish does not make water impure. (3) Regarding fly and flea: From Abu Hurairah: The Prophet said: If a fly falls into the vessel of one of you, immerse it completely then remove it, for in one wing is cure and in the other disease. (Bukhari, Kitab al-Tibb, Bab idha waqa' al-dhubab fi al-ina', no. 5782) The hadith commands immersing the whole fly; if it made food or water impure, he would not have commanded that. (4) Regarding scorpion: From Ibrahim: He saw no harm in scorpion and beetle and every creature without flowing blood. (Musannaf, Bab fi al-khunfasa' wa al-dhubab yaqa'u fi al-ina', no. 652) This shows scorpion has no blood. Principle: Necessity brings ease. This principle emanates from the hadith of the cat: From Kabshah bint Ka'b: Abu Qatadah entered and she poured water for his wudu; a cat came to drink and he tilted the vessel for it. She was amazed; he said: The Messenger of Allah said it is not impure; it is among those who go around you. (Tirmidhi, no. 92; Abu Dawud, no. 75) Cat's meat is haram, so its leftover should be pure, but due to necessity it is makruh.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof passage discussing two categories of impurities that do not spoil well water: (1) bird droppings (pigeon and sparrow), and (2) dead animals without flowing blood (fish, frog, bedbug, fly, etc.). The author first states the general principle: if impurities fall into a well in such quantity that a normal observer would consider it excessive (e.g., every bucket contains dung), only then does it become impure; otherwise, it remains pure. This is based on the hadith of Bir Bada'ah, where impurities regularly fell but the Prophet declared the water pure due to necessity. The commentary then provides proofs from the statements of Tabi'un (successors) like Hasan al-Basri and Hammad to show that bird droppings are either pure or at most disliked, not inherently impure. For animals without flowing blood, the primary proof is the hadith: 'Every food and drink into which falls an animal without blood and dies therein, it is lawful to eat, drink, and perform wudu with it.' Additional proofs include the hadith on seawater (its dead are lawful) and the hadith on immersing a fly. The passage ends with the cat hadith to illustrate the principle that necessity relaxes the general rule. The Hanafi position is thus: well water is not spoiled by bird droppings or by animals without flowing blood, even if they die in it, due to necessity (the difficulty of avoiding such impurities in wells).

Key Terms
استكثار (istiksār): The judgment of a normal observer that the amount of impurity falling into the well is excessive (e.g., every bucket contains dung).
خرء الحمام والعصفور (khar' al-ḥamām wa al-'uṣfūr): Droppings of pigeons and sparrows (domesticated birds).
ما لا دم له (mā lā dama lahu): Creatures without flowing blood (e.g., insects, fish, frogs).
ضرورت (ḍarūrah): Necessity; the difficulty of avoiding such impurities in wells justifies leniency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to well water when a dead scorpion (which has no flowing blood) falls into it?
A) The water becomes impure (najis) and cannot be used for wudu.
B) The water remains pure (tahir) and can be used for wudu.
C) The water becomes makruh but still valid for wudu.
D) The water becomes impure only if the scorpion has blood.

Key Takeaway
Well water remains pure from droppings of pigeons/sparrows and from dead animals without flowing blood, based on necessity and explicit hadith.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Animals Without Blood Do Not Impurify Water
Ruling with multiple hadith proofs on animals without blood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on animals without flowing blood dying in water and explain the proofs and underlying principle.

Core Idea
Animals without flowing blood do not render water impure because impurity is tied to flowing blood, not mere death.

This lesson examines a fundamental principle of Hanafi taharah: the distinction between animals with and without flowing blood. Understanding this rule clarifies many everyday scenarios, such as a fly falling into water or a fish dying in a well. We will explore the proofs from the Sunnah that form the basis of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the act (animal without flowing blood dying in water) and the ruling (water remains pure and usable for purification).
This ruling applies to animals like fish, flies, scorpions, etc.
2
Identify the underlying principle
The ruling is based on the principle that only flowing blood is najis. Animals without flowing blood cannot transmit impurity upon death.
This distinguishes Hanafis from other schools that consider any carrion as impure.
3
Analyze the first proof: Hadith of Salman
The hadith states that food/drink into which a bloodless creature falls remains halal for eating, drinking, and wudu. This directly supports the ruling.
The operative phrase 'laysa laha dam' (has no blood) is key.
4
Analyze further proofs: Seawater, fly, and scorpion
Each additional proof (seawater hadith, fly submergence command, athar on scorpion) reinforces the same principle from different angles.
These proofs address specific animals to remove doubt.
5
Acknowledge cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that any animal's death in water renders it impure if the water is little; the Hanafi position is based on the absence of flowing blood.
The difference stems from different definitions of impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في مسائل البئر [۲] دوسری قسم ہے کہ جن جانوروں میں خون نہیں ہے، پانی میں انکے گر کر مرنے سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ مثلا مچھلی، مینڈک، پسو، مکھی، بھڑ اور بچھو پانی میں گر کر مر جائے تو اس سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ وجه (۱) یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ بہتا ہوا خون ناپاک ہے اس لئے جن جانوروں میں بہتا ہوا خون نہ ہو اس کے گرنے سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ قال رسول الله الله یا سلمان كل طعام و شراب وقعت فيه دابة ليس لهـا دم فـمـاتـت فيه فهو حلال اکله و شربه و وضوءه (دارقطنی ، باب کل طعام وقعت فیه دابتہ لیس لهادم ، ج اول ص ۳۳ نمبر ۸۱ سفن للبیھقی ، باب مالا نفس له سائلة اذامات في الماء القليل ، ج اول ص ۳۸۳، نمبر ۱۱۹۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جس جانور میں خون نہ ہو اس کے گرنے سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ (۲) مچھلی کے بارے میں یہ حدیث موجود ہے۔سمع ابا هريرة يقول سأل رجل رسول الله فقال يا رسول الله ! انا نركب البحر و نحمل معنا القليل من الماء فان توضاأنا به عطشنا أفنتوضأ بماء البحر ؟ فقال رسول الله الله هو الطهور ماؤه الحل ميتته ۔(ابوداودشریف، باب الوضوء بماء البحر، ص۲۳ نمبر ۸۳/ ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی ماء البحرانه طهور ، ص ۱۹، نمبر ۶۹ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مردار یعنی مچھلی مرجائے تو پانی پاک رہے گا۔ (۳) مکھی اور پسو کے بارے میں یہ حدیث موجود ہے۔عن ابی ھریرۃان رسول الله صلى الله ل قال اذا وقع الذباب فى اناء احدكم فليغمسه كله ثم ليطرحه فان في احدى جناحيه شفاء وفي الآخر دواء (بخاری شریف، کتاب الطب، باب اذا وقع الذباب فی الا نا ص ۸۶۰ ، جلد ثانی نمبر ۵۷۸۲) حدیث میں پوری مکھی کو برتن میں ڈالنے کے لئے کہا۔ اگر مکھی سے کھانا یا پانی ناپاک ہوتا تو پوری لکھی کو کیسے ڈالنے کے لئے فرماتے ۔(۴) بچھو کے بارے یہ اثر موجود ہے۔ عن ابراهيم انه لم ير بأسا بالعقرب و الخنفساء و كل نفس ليست بسائلة - (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة باب في الخنفساء والذباب يقع في الاناء ، ج اول ص ۶۱ نمبر ۶۵۲) اس میں ہے کہ بچھو میں خون نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کے گرنے سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہو گا۔
Chapter on Well Issues. [2] The second category is that animals which have no blood, their falling into water and dying does not make the water impure. For example, fish, frog, flea, fly, wasp, and scorpion if they fall into water and die, the water does not become impure. Reason (1): This issue is based on the principle that flowing blood is impure. Therefore, animals which do not have flowing blood, their falling does not make the water impure. There is proof in this hadith: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'O Salman, every food and drink into which a creature that has no blood falls and dies in it, then its eating, drinking, and using it for wudu are permissible.' (Darqutni, Bab kullu ta'am waqa'at fihi dabbah laysa laha dam, vol. 1, p. 33, no. 81; Al-Bayhaqi, Bab ma la nafsa lahu sa'ilah idha mata fi al-ma' al-qalil, vol. 1, p. 383, no. 1193) This hadith states that the animal which has no blood, its falling does not make the water impure. (2) Regarding fish, this hadith exists: I heard Abu Hurairah say: A man asked the Messenger of Allah, saying, 'O Messenger of Allah, we travel by sea and carry with us a little water. If we perform wudu with it, we become thirsty. May we perform wudu with seawater?' The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'Its water is purifying, and its dead is permissible.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-wudu' bi ma' al-bahr, p. 23, no. 83; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi ma' al-bahr annahu tahur, p. 19, no. 69) This hadith states that when a dead thing (i.e., a fish) dies, the water remains pure. (3) Regarding fly and flea, this hadith exists: From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'If a fly falls into the vessel of one of you, then let him submerge it completely and then throw it away, for in one of its wings is a cure and in the other is a disease.' (Bukhari, Kitab al-Tibb, Bab idha waqa'a al-dhubab fi al-ina, p. 860, vol. 2, no. 5782) The hadith commands to submerge the entire fly into the vessel. If the fly made the food or water impure, how would he command to put the whole fly in? (4) Regarding scorpion, this athar exists: From Ibrahim that he saw no harm in the scorpion and the beetle and every creature that does not have flowing blood. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab fi al-khunfasa' wa al-dhubab yaqa'u fi al-ina', vol. 1, p. 61, no. 652) This states that the scorpion has no blood, therefore its falling does not make the water impure.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that animals without flowing blood (e.g., fish, frog, flea, fly, wasp, scorpion) do not render water impure when they fall into it and die. The author categorizes this as the second type of animal. The reasoning is grounded in the principle that flowing blood is impure (najis), so animals lacking such blood cannot transfer impurity. Four proofs are cited: (1) A hadith addressed to Salman stating that any food or drink into which a bloodless creature falls and dies remains permissible for consumption, drinking, and ablution. (2) The well-known hadith about seawater being pure and its dead (fish) being halal, indicating that fish's death does not affect the water's purity. (3) The hadith about a fly falling into a vessel: the command to submerge the fly completely implies that the fly does not impurify the contents, otherwise submerging it would spread impurity. (4) An athar from Ibrahim showing that he saw no issue with scorpions and beetles falling into water, again due to absence of flowing blood. The passage establishes that the category of animals without blood is exempt from causing impurity, regardless of whether they die in the water. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school, which distinguishes between animals with and without flowing blood for issues of najasah.

Key Terms
لا نفس له سائلة (la nafsa lahu sa'ilah): An animal that does not have flowing blood; i.e., its blood does not flow when cut.
طهور (tahur): Purifying; water that is itself pure and can purify others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The water remains pure and usable.
C) The water becomes impure only if the fly is wet.
D) The water becomes makruh but not impure.

Key Takeaway
Animals without flowing blood do not impurify water upon death, based on the principle that impurity requires flowing blood.

Cat's Leftover Water and the Principle of Necessity
Ruling on cat's leftover with principle of necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cat's leftover water and explain how the principle of necessity modifies the ruling from pure to makruh.

Core Idea
Necessity (cat's frequent presence) makes its leftover makruh despite its meat being haram.

This passage introduces a key legal principle: necessity creates ease (al-darurah tujzi al-taysir). It applies this to cat's leftover water (su'ri al-hira). Although the cat's meat is haram, its leftover is not impure due to a hadith; however, the Hanafi school classifies it as makruh tanzihi as a concession for frequent presence. Understanding this ruling clarifies how necessity can shift a ruling from its default position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The leftover water (su'ri) after a cat drinks. The Hanafi ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked).
Not impure, but disliked.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith cited: 'إنها ليست بنجس إنما هي من الطوافين عليكم والطوافات' (It is not impure; it is among those who go around you).
Hadith from Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud, zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly negates impurity of the cat itself, implying its leftover is also not impure. However, the Hanafi school adds a qualification: because the cat's meat is haram, the default would be purity, but necessity (frequent presence) makes it makruh.
The proof is zanni al-dalala; the ruling is not qat'i.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider cat's leftover pure (tahir) based on the literal hadith. Hanafis disagree due to the principle of necessity and the cat's haram meat.
Cross-madhhab dispute.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position (makruh tanzihi) is the mufta bihi. It balances the hadith's declaration of purity with the principle of necessity, avoiding full purity due to the cat's forbidden meat.
Compromise between text and maslahah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول : ضرورت کی وجہ سے سہولت ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس حدیث سے یہ اصول مترشح ہوتا ہے۔عن كبشة بنت كعب بن مالك ان ابا قتادة دخل عليها قالت فسكبت له وضوء ا قالت فجائت هرة تشرب فأصغى لها الاناء حتى شربت ، قالت كبشة فرأنى انظر اليه فقال أتعجبين يا ابنة اخى ؟ فقلت نعم قال ان رسول الله علم قال انها ليست بنجس انما هي من الطوافين عليكم والطوافات ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی سوراکھر ق ص ۲۷ نمبر ۹۲ ابوداؤد شریف، باب سؤر الهرة ، ص۱۲، نمبر ۷۵) بلی کا گوشت حرام ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھانا پاک ہونا چاہئے لیکن ضرورت کی وجہ سے اس کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہوا
Principle: Necessity creates ease. From this hadith, this principle emanates. From Kabshah bint Ka'b ibn Malik that Abu Qatadah entered upon her. She said: I poured water for his wudu. She said: Then a cat came to drink, and he tilted the vessel for it until it drank. Kabshah said: He saw me looking at him and said: Do you wonder, O daughter of my brother? I said: Yes. He said: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'Indeed it (the cat) is not impure; it is only among those who go around you (i.e., are frequently present).' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi su'ri al-hirah, p. 27, no. 92; Abu Dawud, Bab su'ri al-hirah, p. 12, no. 75) The cat's meat is haram, so its leftover should have been pure, but due to necessity, its leftover became makruh.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage introduces the principle that necessity brings about ease (al-darurah tujzi al-taysir). It then cites a hadith about a cat drinking from a vessel used for wudu. The cat is among animals that are frequently around humans, and the Prophet declared it not impure. However, the author notes that since the cat's meat is haram (forbidden), its leftover (su'ri) logically should be pure because impurity is tied to forbidden flesh. But due to the necessity of cats being frequently around, the ruling is that cat's leftover is makruh (disliked) rather than pure. This demonstrates how necessity can modify a ruling from pure to makruh as a concession. The principle extracted is that necessity can create ease in rulings.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'ri): The leftover water or drink after an animal has drunk from it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the cat's meat is haram, and necessity of frequent presence makes it makruh.
C) Because the hadith says it is impure.
D) Because the Prophet forbade using cat's leftover.

Key Takeaway
Cat's leftover water is not impure but is makruh tanzihi in the Hanafi school, demonstrating how necessity can relax a ruling.

Person or Edible Animal Falling into a Well: Water Remains Pure
Ruling with proof on water purity from a living being falling into a well

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water purity when a human or edible animal falls into a well and comes out alive, and explain the reasoning based on the absence of impurity.

Core Idea
A living being does not impurify water unless it brings visible impurity from outside.

This lesson addresses a common concern in daily life: what happens to well water if a person or an animal falls in? The Hanafi ruling provides clarity: the water remains pure as long as no external impurity is present. We will examine the ruling, its condition, and the rational proof behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Subject
What is the ruling on the water? Who does it apply to? The passage clearly states that water does not become impure by the falling of a human or an animal whose meat is eaten, provided they come out alive.
The ruling covers both humans and halal animals.
2
State the Condition
The ruling is conditional: there must be no impurity (najasa) on the body of the being that fell. If there is any visible impurity, the water becomes impure.
This condition is crucial; the ruling does not apply to a person who has feces or blood on them.
3
Identify the Proof (Dalil)
The text gives a rational proof: the human or animal itself is not impure (not najis al-ayn), and since no external impurity is present, the water remains pure. This is based on the principle that impurity transfers only through actual contact with a physical impurity.
This is a dalil aqli (rational evidence) based on the inherent purity of humans and edible animals.
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Context
This ruling is agreed upon within the Hanafi school but may differ in other schools which might consider the mere presence of a living being as a potential source of impurity. The Hanafi position requires visible impurity.
Understanding this difference helps in fiqh comparisons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في مسائل البئر (۳۲) ولا بوقوع آدمى وما يؤكل لحمه اذا خرج حيًّا ولم يكن على بدنه نجاسة لغت: خرء: بیٹ ۔ حمام : كبوتر عصفور : چڑیا۔۔ ضفدع: مینڈک ۔ بق : پسو کھٹل۔ ذباب بکھی۔ زنبور: بھڑ۔ عقرب: بچھو۔ ترجمه : (۳۲) اور آدمی کنواں میں گر جائے ، یا جس جانور کا گوشت کھایا جاتا ہو وہ گر جائے اور زندہ نکل آئے تو پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا،اگر اس کے بدن پر نجاست نہ ہو۔ تشریح : ایسا آدمی جسکے بدن پر نجاست نہ ہو، یا ایسا جانور جس کا گوشت کھایا جاتا ہو وہ کنواں میں گھس جائے یا گر جائے اور زندہ نکل آئے تو اس سے کنواں ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ وجه : اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس کے جسم پر نجاست نہیں ہے، اور یہ خود بھی ناپاک نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کے گرنے سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔
Chapter on Well Issues. (32) Nor [does water become impure] by the falling of a human or an animal whose meat is eaten, if it comes out alive and there is no impurity on its body. Vocabulary: khur' : excrement; hammam: pigeon; 'usfur: sparrow; dafda': frog; baqq: flea; dhubab: fly; zunbur: wasp; 'aqrab: scorpion. Translation (32): If a human falls into a well, or an animal whose meat is eaten falls and comes out alive, then the water does not become impure, provided that there is no impurity on its body. Commentary: Such a human who has no impurity on his body, or such an animal whose meat is eaten, if it enters or falls into a well and comes out alive, then the well does not become impure. Reason: The reason is that there is no impurity on its body, and it itself is not impure, therefore its falling does not make the water impure.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This ruling states that if a human or an animal whose meat is halal (e.g., sheep, cow, chicken) falls into a well and comes out alive, the water remains pure as long as no actual impurity (najasah) was on its body. The reasoning is that the human or such animal is not inherently impure (najis al-'ayn), and without external impurity, no impurity is transferred to the water. This is based on the principle that only the presence of a physical impurity (like blood, urine, or feces) impurifies water, not the mere presence of a living being. The glossary preceding the commentary defines key terms for the well chapter, including names of various animals, but the commentary focuses on the legal point.

Key Terms
آدمى (adami): Human being.
ما يؤكل لحمه (ma yu'kalu lahmuhu): Animals whose meat is permissible to eat (halal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a sheep falls into a well and comes out alive without any impurity on its body, what is the ruling on the water?
A) The water becomes impure because the sheep is an animal.
B) The water remains pure.
C) The water becomes impure if the sheep is wet.
D) The water becomes makruh.

Key Takeaway
Water remains pure when a human or edible animal falls in alive and exits without visible impurity, because they are inherently pure and only actual najasah transfers impurity.

Donkey, Mule, and Predators Falling into a Well: The Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on donkey, mule, predatory birds and wild beasts falling into well

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a donkey, mule, or predatory bird/beast falls into a well and identify the conditions under which the water remains pure.

Core Idea
Water remains pure unless actual impurity (saliva, urine, feces) enters it, regardless of the animal's meat being haram.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from Hanafi fiqh regarding animals that fall into wells. Many assume that any animal whose meat is haram automatically impurifies the water. The Hanafi school, however, distinguishes between inherent impurity (najasah) and mere legal prohibition (hurmat al-akl). We will explore the conditions and proofs for water remaining pure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the falling of a donkey, mule, predatory bird, or wild beast into a well. The ruling is that the water does not become impure according to the correct madhhab (fi al-sahih).
2
List the required conditions
For the water to remain pure, the following conditions must be met: the animal exits alive; the water does not reach its mouth; its saliva does not enter the water; and it does not urinate or defecate in the water.
If any condition is violated, the water becomes impure.
3
Understand the reasoning
These animals are not inherently impure (najis al-ayn); only actual physical impurities (najasah) like saliva, urine, or feces transfer impurity. Their meat being haram does not make them najis al-ayn.
Compare with pigs and dogs, which are najis al-ayn.
4
Examine the proofs
The passage cites two proofs: (a) Ibn Abbas's statement that there is no janabah on water, implying contact alone does not impurify; (b) 'Ata's response that a junub's hand entering water forgetfully causes no harm. These support the analogy that animals without inherent impurity do not impurify water.
Dalil: Qawl Sahabi (Ibn Abbas) and Athar of 'Ata.
5
Extract the underlying principle
The passage concludes: water becomes impure only when actual impurity enters it. This is a general principle in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۳) ولا بوقوع بغل و حمار وسباع طير ووحش في الصحيح ترجمه :(۳۳) گدھا، خچر ، شکار کرنے والے پرندے اور وحشی درندے کے گرنے سے صحیح مذھب کے مطابق پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ تشریح : جن جانور کا گوشت مشکوک ہے، جیسے گدھا اور خچر ، یا اس کا گوشت حرام ہے لیکن وہ نجس العین نہیں ہے، جیسے پھاڑ کھانے والے پرندے، یاوحشی جانور، یہ جانور کنواں میں گر جائے، اور زندہ نکل آئے ، اور پانی اس کے منہ تک نہ پہنچا ہو اور نہ اس کا لعاب پانی میں گرا ہو، اور نہ اس نے پانی میں پیشاب یا پاخانہ کیا تو پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ وجه : (۱) ان جانوروں کا گوشت اگر چہ حرام ہے لیکن اس کے جسم پر نجاست نہیں ہے، اور نہ اس نے پیشاب، یا پاخانہ کیا اور نہ اس کا ناپاک تھوک پانی میں گیا تو پانی میں کوئی ناپاکی نہیں گئی اس لئے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ (۲) عـن ابـن عبـاس قـال ليـس على الثوب جنابة ، و لا على الارض جنابة و لا على الرجل يمسه الجنب جنابة و ليس على الماء جنابة يقول اذا سبقته يده فادخلهما فى الماء و هو جنب قبل ان يغسلهما فلا بأس - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الماء یمسه الجب اویدخله، ج اول ص اے، نمبر ۳۰۹) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ اگر ہاتھ پر نجاست نہ ہو تو جنبی آدمی کے ہاتھ ڈالنے سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہو گا اسی پر قیاس کر کے ان جانور کے گرنے سے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا ۔ (۳) سألت عطاء عن الجنب ينسى فيدخل يده في الاناء الذي فيه غسله قبل أن يغسلها قال ان نسى فلا بأس فليغسل يديه (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الماء يمسه الحب اوید خلہ، ج اول ص اے نمبر ۳۰۸) اس اثر میں بھی ہے کہ ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔ اصول: جب تک نا پا کی پانی میں نہ جائے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔
(33) Nor [does water become impure] by the falling of a mule, donkey, predatory birds, and wild beasts, according to the correct [madhhab]. Translation (33): According to the correct madhhab, the water does not become impure by the falling of a donkey, mule, predatory birds, and wild beasts. Commentary: Animals whose meat is doubtful, such as donkey and mule, or whose meat is haram but they are not inherently impure (najis al-'ayn), such as predatory birds and wild beasts—if these animals fall into a well, come out alive, and the water does not reach their mouth, and their saliva does not fall into the water, and they do not urinate or defecate in the water, then the water does not become impure. Reason (1): Although the meat of these animals is haram, there is no impurity on their body, and they did not urinate or defecate, and their impure saliva did not go into the water, so no impurity entered the water, therefore the water does not become impure. (2) From Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'There is no janabah on a garment, nor janabah on the earth, nor janabah on a man touched by a janib, nor is there janabah on water. He said: If his hand precedes him and he puts it into water while in a state of janabah before washing it, there is no harm.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-ma' yamasuhu al-junub aw yudkhiluhu, vol. 1, p. ?, no. 309) This saying of the Companion indicates that if there is no impurity on the hand, then the water does not become impure by the entry of a junub's hand. By analogy (qiyas), the falling of these animals does not make the water impure. (3) I asked 'Ata about a junub who forgets and puts his hand into the vessel containing his washing water before washing his hands. He said: If he forgets, there is no harm; let him wash his hands.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-ma' yamasuhu al-junub aw yudkhiluhu, vol. 1, p. ?, no. 308) This athar also indicates that it does not become impure. Principle: As long as no impurity enters the water, the water does not become impure.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This ruling addresses animals that are either doubtful (like donkey and mule regarding permissibility of meat) or haram but not inherently impure (najis al-'ayn) such as predatory birds and wild beasts. The correct Hanafi position (fi al-sahih) is that the water does not become impure if such an animal falls in and comes out alive, provided three conditions: (1) the water did not reach the animal's mouth (so no saliva mixes), (2) the animal's saliva did not drop into the water, and (3) the animal did not urinate or defecate in the water. The reasoning is that these animals are not inherently impure; only actual physical impurities (najasah) like urine, feces, or blood would impurify the water. The passage then provides two proofs from the practice of the Salaf: (a) the statement of Ibn Abbas regarding a junub person's hand entering water—if the hand has no impurity, the water remains pure. This is applied by analogy (qiyas) to the animals. (b) The response of 'Ata' that if a junub forgetfully puts his hand into water, there is no harm, again indicating that mere contact does not impurify. Finally, a principle is stated: water becomes impure only when actual impurity enters it.

Key Terms
سباع طير ووحش (siba' tayr wa wahsh): Predatory birds (e.g., hawks, eagles) and wild beasts (e.g., wolves, lions).
نجس العين (najis al-'ayn): Inherently impure, like pigs and dogs, whose very essence is considered impure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always, regardless of conditions.
B) Only if the donkey did not urinate or defecate in the water and its saliva did not enter.
C) Only if the water is more than two qullahs.
D) Never, because donkey meat is haram.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, water does not become impure from a non-najis al-ayn animal falling in unless actual najasah (saliva, urine, feces) enters the water.

Ruling on a Human or Edible Animal Falling into a Well
Ruling on well purity with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the purity of well water when a human or edible animal falls in, and list the three conditions that must be satisfied for the water to remain pure.

Core Idea
A well does not become impure from a pure being; impurity requires actual filth.

This short passage from the chapter on well water addresses a common scenario: a person or an animal falling into a well. The ruling is clear but depends on specific conditions. We will examine these conditions and the underlying reasoning to understand when water remains pure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the fall of a human or edible animal into a well. The ruling: the water does not become impure.
The ruling is a negative statement: 'لا' (it is not impure).
2
List the conditions
The ruling applies only when three conditions are met: the falling being must be a human or halal meat animal; it must exit alive; its body must be free of visible impurity.
If any condition is missing, the water becomes impure.
3
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The reason given is that the being itself is not impure and there is no actual filth on it. Impurity requires a tangible najasah to transfer.
This reasoning (talil) is a rational proof, not a textual one.
4
Recognize what violates the ruling
If the being dies in the well, or has visible impurity on its body (even if alive), the water becomes impure. Also, if the animal is not edible (e.g., pig, carnivore), the ruling may not apply.
These cases are not explicitly in the passage but are derived from the conditions.

Chapter on matters of the well. (32) And it is not [impure] by the falling of a human and what is eaten of its meat, if it comes out alive and there is no impurity on its body. Vocabulary: ... Translation: (32) And if a person falls into the well, or an animal whose meat is eaten falls, and it comes out alive, then the water does not become impure, if there is no impurity on its body. Explanation: Such a person who has no impurity on his body, or such an animal whose meat is eaten enters or falls into the well and comes out alive, then the well does not become impure. Reason: The reason is that there is no impurity on his body, and he himself is also not impure, so the water does not become impure by his falling.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the section on well water. It states that if a human being or an animal whose meat is permissible to eat falls into a well and comes out alive, the water does not become impure provided that there is no physical impurity on their body. The author explains that the reason for this is that the impurity of water requires the presence of an actual impure substance. Since the person or animal is not intrinsically impure and has no filth on their body, their mere fall does not contaminate the water. The Urdu commentary expands on this, emphasizing the condition of the body being free from impurity.

Key Terms
آدمى (Ādamī): A human being, as a species, not specifically a Muslim or non-Muslim.
ما يؤكل لحمه (Mā yu'kalu laḥmuhu): Animals whose meat is permissible to eat according to Islamic law (halal).
نجاسة (Najāsah): Any physically impure substance (such as urine, blood, feces) that is perceptible on the body.

When Donkeys, Mules, and Wild Animals Fall into a Well
Extends the ruling to animals with haram meat, with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling and conditions for a well remaining pure when non-edible animals fall in, and explain the proof from the sayings of Ibn Abbas and Ata.

Core Idea
Water remains pure unless a tangible impurity actually enters; the animal's haram meat does not transmit impurity.

This lesson extends the ruling on water purity to animals whose meat is not eaten (like donkeys, mules) or is haram but not intrinsically impure (like birds of prey and wild animals). You will see how the Hanafi school applies the principle that impurity requires physical transfer, and supports it with analogical reasoning from the case of a junub's hand.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals covered
List the animals mentioned: donkeys, mules (meat doubtful), birds of prey, and wild animals (meat haram but not najis al-ayn).
Note that the ruling is for animals whose meat is not permissible or is questionable.
2
State the conditions for purity
The water remains pure if: the animal exits alive, its saliva does not enter the water, it does not urinate or defecate, and the water has not reached its mouth.
These conditions ensure no impurity actually mixes with the water.
3
Understand the reasoning
The animal's body is not intrinsically impure (najis al-ayn); only if actual impurity (saliva, urine, feces) enters the water does it become impure.
Haram meat does not equal najis in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Examine the proof via qiyas
The text cites sayings of Ibn Abbas and Ata that water does not become impure by the entry of a junub's clean hand. By analogy, these animals (whose bodies are free of impurity) also do not affect the water.
Qiyas from the case of a junub's hand to these animals is valid because the common illa is the absence of tangible impurity.

(33) And it is not [impure] by the falling of a mule and a donkey and birds of prey and wild animals, according to the correct [view]. Translation: (33) Donkey, mule, birds of prey, and wild beasts falling into the well, according to the correct view, the water does not become impure. Explanation: The meat of these animals is either doubtful (mashkuk), like donkey and mule, or haram but not intrinsically impure (najis al-'ayn), like birds of prey and wild animals. If these animals fall into the well and come out alive, and the water has not reached its mouth, and its saliva has not fallen into the water, and it has not urinated or defecated in the water, then the water does not become impure. Reason: (1) Even though their meat is haram, there is no impurity on their body, and they did not urinate, defecate, or drop their impure saliva into the water, so no impurity entered the water; therefore the water is not impure. (2) From Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) he said: 'There is no impurity on a garment, and no impurity on the earth, and no impurity on a person who touches a junub, and no impurity on water. He said: If his hand precedes him and he puts them in the water while he is junub before washing them, there is no harm.' This saying of the Companion indicates that if there is no impurity on the hand, the water does not become impure by the entry of the hand of a junub. By analogy (qiyas), the water does not become impure by the falling of these animals. (3) I asked 'Ata' about a junub who forgets and puts his hand in the vessel containing his water for ghusl before washing it. He said: If he forgot, there is no harm; he should wash his hands. This effect also indicates that it does not become impure. Principle: As long as no impurity enters the water, the water does not become impure.

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling to animals whose meat is not permissible to eat, such as donkeys, mules, birds of prey, and wild animals. The author clarifies that the water remains pure if the animal exits alive and no actual impurity (like saliva, urine, or feces) enters the water. The commentary provides two proofs from the sayings of Companions (Ibn Abbas and 'Ata'), showing that the principle is that water is not rendered impure by the mere entry of a living being unless there is tangible impurity. The phrase 'fi al-sahih' indicates that this is the preferred view within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
سباع طير (Sibāʿ ṭayr): Birds of prey that catch and eat other animals, such as eagles, hawks, etc.
وحش (Waḥsh): Wild animals that are not domesticated, including predators.
مشكوک (Mashkūk): Doubtful; referring to the status of the animal's saliva or meat where the ruling is not clearly pure or impure.
نجس العين (Najis al-'ayn): Intrinsically impure; the very substance of the thing is considered impure in Islamic law.

Water Takes the Ruling of the Saliva
States principle with illustrative examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of water when mixed with the saliva of various animals according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The purity of water follows the ruling of the saliva that mixes into it.

This passage introduces a key principle in Hanafi taharah: the water's ruling is determined by the ruling of the animal's saliva that mixes into it. The type of animal—human, edible, wild, donkey/mule, or cat—dictates whether the saliva is pure, impure, doubtful, or makruh, and the water acquires that same status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
Understand that the Arabic phrase 'akhadha hukmahu' means the water takes the exact legal ruling of the saliva that mixes with it. This is a direct causal relationship.
The principle applies when the saliva actually reaches the water, not merely proximity.
2
Classify animals by saliva ruling
Based on Hanafi fiqh, list the five categories given: human (pure), edible animal (pure), wild animal (impure), donkey/mule (doubtful), cat (makruh).
These categories are specific; not all animals are covered here.
3
Apply the principle to each category
For pure saliva, water remains pure and no action needed. For impure saliva, water becomes impure and the entire well must be emptied. For doubtful, water is doubtful; for makruh, water is makruh.
The consequence varies: only impure requires emptying the well entirely.
4
Recognize practical implications
If a wild animal falls into a well, the water becomes impure and cannot be used for worship until the well is emptied. For doubtful cases, further investigation may be needed.
This affects daily taharah practices.

Vocabulary: sabāʿ: predator; sabāʿ ṭayr: bird of prey; waḥshī: wild animal. Translation: (34) And if the saliva of the fallen [animal] reaches the water, it takes its ruling. (34) The animal that has fallen into the water, its saliva reaches the water, then the ruling of the water will be the ruling of its saliva. Explanation: Whatever ruling the saliva of the animal that fell into the well has, if that saliva mixes with the water, then that water will have the same ruling. For example: [1] The saliva of a human is pure, and the saliva of an animal whose meat is eaten is pure; if this saliva mixes with the well water, the well remains pure because the saliva is pure. [2] And the saliva of a wild animal is impure, so if its saliva mixes with the water, the water becomes impure, and the entire well must be emptied. [3] The saliva of a donkey and mule is doubtful (mashkūk), so if their saliva mixes, the water becomes doubtful. [4] The saliva of a cat is makrūh, so if its saliva mixes, the water becomes makrūh. This is the meaning of 'takes its ruling'.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage explains that when saliva from an animal that has fallen into the well reaches the water, the water takes the ruling of that saliva. The author provides examples: human saliva and that of edible animals are pure, so the water remains pure; wild animal saliva is impure, so the water becomes impure; donkey and mule saliva is doubtful; cat saliva is makruh. Thus, the effect on the water depends entirely on the ruling of the animal's saliva. The vocabulary list at the beginning defines terms used in this and previous lessons.

Key Terms
لعاب (Luʿāb): Saliva or drool of an animal that may carry impurity.
اخذ حكمه (Akhadha ḥukmahu): Takes its ruling; i.e., the water acquires the same legal status as the saliva that mixes with it.

Determining the Time of Impurity from a Dead Animal in a Well
Provides a method to determine from when the well became impure based on the state of the dead animal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule to determine the presumptive time of impurity (najasa) of well water when a dead animal is found, based on its state (swollen or not).

Core Idea
A fresh dead animal in a well makes water impure from one day prior; a swollen one from three days prior, based on customary observation.

When a dead animal is discovered in a well and the exact time of its fall is unknown, Islamic law provides a method to determine the retroactive start of impurity. This ruling relies on observable signs of decomposition and the principle of caution (ihtiyat). Understanding this helps in correctly assessing the validity of past acts of purification and prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that finding a dead animal in a well renders the water najis (impure). The ruling is that the water cannot be used for purification.
2
Determine the state of the animal
Check whether the animal is swollen (muntafikh) or not. This observable sign is key to the presumptive time.
Swelling indicates the animal has been dead for at least three days.
3
Apply the presumptive timeline
If the animal is not swollen, the water is considered impure from one day and one night prior. If swollen, from three days and three nights prior.
This timeline is used only when the actual time of falling is unknown.
4
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The reasoning is based on customary observation: a fresh carcass typically floats after one day, and swelling occurs after three days. Caution (ihtiyat) dictates using these defaults.
The reasoning is from 'urf (custom) and not a direct textual proof.
5
Note the consequence
Anyone who performed wudu or ghusl with that water during the presumed period must repeat their prayers, as the purification was invalid.
The well should be emptied and cleaned to remove impurity.

Source Text
